[2025-11-23T21:53:30Z] Akshay: The origin of the use of this prefix letter ‘X’  (single letter not X) likely dates back to the International Radiotelegraph Convention at London in 1912. There the International Telecommunication Union (ITU) assigned the  ‘X’ series to denote the ownership of Y (one word) by Commonwealth nations, in honor of Queen Victoria. Countries with two-letter Y markings starting with the letter ‘X’ include India, Australia, Seychelles, Bermuda and Gibraltar, among others. Notably, this convention has continued even after independence. The government of India however maintains, as late as  2021 in a response to a question asked in Parliament, that there is no colonial significance to the specific two-letter combination for India, though it claims to be studying the possibility of changing this to more ‘Indian’ letter pairs. ↵ Id X, Y. Bonus for ID’ing the two-letter combo used by India.
